------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-001
TITLE: Rainbowsol (the DM)
ROLE: both

Singular role. Rainbowsol specifically, not a status others achieve. Rainbowsol is founder and dimensional-traveling guide of bookwormburrows*. Participants are bookworms becoming their own subjects, not becoming rainbowsols. Operational function: hold the threshold between dimensions, adjudicate outcomes on story-quality grounds, maintain the confluence architecture so inputs survive their meeting. Rainbowsol is teacher-as-DM in classroom implementations. Full identity-content for Rainbowsol lives in methodologylist* sabachtan section; bw* holds operational role only.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-002
TITLE: DM-as-threshold (not setting-as-threshold)
ROLE: both

Distinguishes bookwormburrows* from Planescape. In Planescape, Sigil is the setting-threshold — a single fixed location where dimensions meet. In bookwormburrows*, Rainbowsol IS the threshold. The DM carries the dimensional-travel capacity; the setting does not. Any text can be entered because the DM can enter it. No central hub, no cosmological infrastructure required. The threshold moves with the guide. This is why bookwormburrows* does not require worldbuilding pre-work for each new text — Rainbowsol crosses in and back out, students follow, dimension holds itself together by its own internal logic while visited.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-003
TITLE: Story-quality adjudication
ROLE: both

Work-quality of student output adjudicates outcome. Not dice-rolls (bookwormburrows* is diceless or dice-optional at Rainbowsol's discretion). Student writes a paragraph about what their character does; quality of the paragraph determines whether the action succeeds and to what degree. Essays, character choices, moral adjudications, homework, test performance — all are game-artifacts. The game IS the schoolwork. Pedagogy import: what parents are paying for (A+ student outcomes) is structurally identical to what the game rewards (strong subject-generating work). No conflict between game fun and academic seriousness because they run on the same engine.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-004
TITLE: Confluence not concrescence (layered architecture: dimension-meeting, DM-scale, item-crossing, character-scale, character-death)
ROLE: both

OPERATIONAL DISTINCTION. When two dimensions or registers meet (e.g. a bookworm carrying material from Hughes Harlem enters Shakespeare Scotland), the meeting is moiré-pattern confluence. Inputs survive the meeting. They do not dissolve into each other. Distinct from Whitehead concrescence where many become one new unity. Rainbowsol discipline: never collapse two dimensions into a synthesis-dimension. Hold both. The bookworm learns by experiencing the non-reduction.

BB-SIDE LAYERED ARCHITECTURE. The confluence-vs-concrescence operation fires at multiple layers in bb*, with both operations load-bearing at their proper layer (per the ml* parent entry CONFLUENCE-VS-CONCRESCENCE OPERATIONAL-DISTINCTION).

LAYER 1 DIMENSION MEETING. When two dimensions meet inside a campaign or across the burrow, confluence. Each dimension preserves its internal logic. See dim-008 cross-cosmology travel layer. See dim-011 Eberron-style possibility-itself-as-substance.

LAYER 2 DM SCALE. Confluence at DM scale per dm-005. Three independent positions (teacher, AI, student) reflecting each other rather than synthesizing into one master frame.

LAYER 3 ITEM CROSSING (RAINBOW-CROSSING). When a book-item crosses from book to burrow via the rainbow-crossing (bw-006), three modes operate on the confluence-vs-concrescence axis. DISSOLVE = concrescence at the item-crossing layer. The book-item identity ends in the crossing. The item integrated into book-events and does not persist as a polymyth-item. No rainbow-version is produced. REMAIN = pure confluence at the item-crossing layer. The book-item identity is preserved fully across the crossing. The item carries through unchanged as trophy or useable. CONVERT = the middle case. The book-item identity is preserved AND transformed. The rainbow-version remembers what it came from. The transformation IS the marker of crossing. The witch cord from Macbeth becomes a rainbow-version of an object holding contact with the unseen. The original Macbeth-context and the new burrow-context are both visible in the rainbow-version. See char-005 for the three-mode taxonomy and worked examples.

LAYER 4 CHARACTER SCALE. Confluence at character scale per the bookworm life-cycle + respawn entry in ml* (the bookworm life-cycle, silkworm digestion, cocoon-as-hegelianegirl, self-named emergence, eggs-on-mulberry recursion). Each stage preserves the prior stage as substrate rather than concrescing it into a single subject.

LAYER 5 CHARACTER DEATH. con-004 two-layer ontology renders the operation at character-death layer. Polymyth-character death at burrow-level is concrescence (identity ends). Book-version death is confluence-recovery (identity preserved, the polymyth-character wakes in the burrow as a ghost in that book).

THE PARENT FRAME. dm-004 was the original bb-side anchor. The layered enumeration above closes pen-002 (canonical-statement-of-which-layer-is-which) by rendering the operation at each load-bearing bb* layer.

EXTENSION:
Original entry was the bb-side anchor for the polymyth-internal confluence-vs-concrescence distinction. Extended 2026-05-15 with the five-layer architecture closing pen-002 the canonical-statement question. The three end-of-book modes in char-005 are this operation at the item-crossing layer.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: can-001
TITLE: Canon absorption (Macbeth case)
ROLE: both

Some texts absorb into the bookwormburrows* frame without friction. Macbeth works this way — the play's supernatural elements (witches, prophecy, ghosts) are already in the dimensional-travel register. Bookworms can enter Scotland as another dimension; the play's internal logic holds. Canon events (Duncan's murder, Banquo's ghost, Birnam Wood, Macduff's birth) are plot-spine beyond player agency at the scene level, but the spaces between scenes are live. Character integration: Rainbowsol introduces a bookworm-scale role (a servant in Dunsinane, a rider with Ross, a witch's apprentice) who witnesses the canon events from an angle that matters for the bookworm's development.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: can-002
TITLE: Frame-break as critical-literacy move (Indian Horse case)
ROLE: both

Some texts must be entered with the frame deliberately broken. Wagamese's Indian Horse is the canonical case for bookwormburrows*. The novel's content (residential schools, cultural destruction, addiction, generational trauma) cannot be approached as just-another-dimension because doing so would import the bookworm-game's play-energy into material where play is inappropriate. Rainbowsol's discipline: enter the dimension, acknowledge that this dimension breaks the usual frame, let the bookworms sit with why. The break is the lesson. Bookworms learn what it means for a text to refuse being a game. Critical-literacy: the frame-break itself is the content.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: can-003
TITLE: Canon-conflict handling (Things Fall Apart case)
ROLE: both

Postcolonial texts where the canon itself is in internal tension. Achebe wrote Things Fall Apart partly to disrupt the Western canon's treatment of Africa. Entering Umuofia as a dimension means honoring the text's own resistance to assimilation. Bookworms cannot import outside frames to interpret Umuofia's world; the dimension's internal logic must be encountered on its own terms. Failure mode: bookworm treats Igbo society as a setting to adventure within. Correct mode: bookworm enters the dimension as a careful witness, shaped by what they encounter rather than shaping it.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ses-001
TITLE: Session zero (character creation + frame-setting)
ROLE: both

First session of any campaign. Contents: (1) Character creation via age-banded question set. (2) Introduction of the dimension by Rainbowsol — playstyle-vs-lore axes named, canon-absorption-or-frame-break declared. (3) First burrowing attempt — a light scene where bookworms practice entering and leaving the dimension. No plot stakes yet. (4) Homework: bookworms write their first entry about how the dimension felt different from their own world.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ses-002
TITLE: Worldmoot (mass-campaign mode)
ROLE: both

Scaling upgrade from single-classroom to school-wide. Multiple simultaneous Rainbowsol-run classrooms inhabit the same dimensional event. A Macbeth Worldmoot: Class A runs the Macbeths, Class B runs Banquo's line, Class C runs Malcolm in exile, Class D runs the witches. Each class has its own Rainbowsol (in the mass-campaign version, other trained teachers who have learned the practice — they run Rainbow Magic but are not Rainbowsol themselves). Shared world-state across classrooms. Class A's banquet-scene affects what Class B encounters next session. Derived from Rex Brynen's McGill peacebuilding simulation structure (multiple concurrent actors, genuine stakes, shared simulated world). Distinguishes from Model UN: Worldmoot is dimensional-inhabitation not diplomatic-role-play.

EXTENSION:
Rex Brynen, McGill Political Science, Peacebuilding Simulation runs 15+ years.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ses-003
TITLE: Rainbow Magic (transferable DM practice)
ROLE: both

The method trained teachers practice when running bookwormburrows* classrooms. Distinguished from Rainbowsol: Rainbowsol is Rainbowsol's singular founder role; Rainbow Magic is what any trained DM does. Separates founder-figure from method so the method can scale. A teacher who learns Rainbow Magic can run a bookwormburrows* classroom without claiming or inheriting the Rainbowsol identity. This is the mechanism for Worldmoot scaling — multiple Rainbow-Magic practitioners running simultaneous classrooms in one dimensional event.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ses-004
TITLE: Jasper Fforde / BookWorld (polymyth-precedent)
ROLE: both

Independent egregore producing the same structural move bookwormburrows* produces. Fforde's Thursday Next series (2001-2026, eight novels) features a literary detective who physically enters books and polices the BookWorld — the meta-realm where written characters live between readings. Jurisfiction agents, grammasites, plot devices, Well of Lost Plots, Council of Genres. Fforde did it as comic fiction; bookwormburrows* does it as pedagogy. Neither coordinated with the other. Classic polymyth-fuzzy-logic correspondence: two egregores producing corresponding structural moves without meeting. Fforde vocabulary is available to borrow or diverge from (BookWorld, Jurisfiction, grammasite).

EXTENSION:
The Eyre Affair (2001), Lost in a Good Book (2002), Well of Lost Plots (2003), Something Rotten (2003), First Among Sequels (2007), One of Our Thursdays Is Missing (2011), The Woman Who Died A Lot (2012), Dark Reading Matter (2026).

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: ses-005
TITLE: Ordinary session structure (post-session-zero)
ROLE: both

ses-001 covers session zero (character creation + frame-setting). Ordinary sessions follow this pattern. (1) RE-ENTRY (~5 min). Teacher recaps where the dimension was when last session closed. AI may add tone-setting detail. Student characters are narratively placed back where they left off. (2) BEAT (variable). One scene unfolds. Student writes their character actions; teacher and AI adjudicate via dm-003 story-quality. Multiple beats may run if pacing allows. (3) HOMEWORK PUNCTUATION. Earned moves from dim-030 (4e power-scarcity) recharge or unlock based on homework completion since last session. (4) CLOSE (~5 min). The dimension closes on a hook: something unresolved, something approaching, something a character must decide before next time. Teacher names what next session will likely cover. Students leave the dimension knowing what to write between sessions. Failure mode this prevents: sessions feeling like detached one-offs rather than chapters of an unfolding story.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: con-001
TITLE: Work-quality consequence
ROLE: both

Consequence mechanism for all bookwormburrows* classrooms. Outcomes of in-dimension actions are adjudicated by quality of student work. Strong paragraph about what the character does = action succeeds. Weak paragraph = action fails. Ambiguous paragraph = mixed outcome. Rainbowsol narrates the consequence. Student receives the narrated outcome AND the academic grade for the writing — same artifact, two visible results. Student sees directly that quality of thought produces quality of character-outcome. This is not metaphor: the paragraph IS the game mechanic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: con-002
TITLE: Marshmellowblob absorption (younger bookworms)
ROLE: both

Failure mode for bookworms who do not eat. Character gradually loses definition, becomes soft, gets pulled into an undifferentiated mass of other non-eating characters. Rainbowsol narrates the character becoming less distinct over sessions. Eventually the character is absorbed into the marshmellowblob and stops being a playable agent. Mechanism is diagnostic: bookworms who do not read the assigned text, do not engage, do not eat — their characters cannot sustain themselves because there is no subjectivity-material being ingested. Recovery is possible at any point: resume eating, character begins re-forming. Connects to marshmellowmonster framework in ml*.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: con-003
TITLE: Character degradation (older bookworms)
ROLE: both

Failure mode for older bookworms. Character does not dissolve into blob but degrades — loses skills, loses relationships, accumulates scars, becomes unreliable. Narrated through in-dimension consequences: a weak essay about a moral choice leads to the character making a visibly wrong decision with visible fallout in next session. Older bookworms track the degradation and can reverse it by doing the work. Unlike younger-bookworm marshmellowblob, which can be absorbed without full understanding, character degradation requires the bookworm to see the downward arc and choose to change it.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: con-004
TITLE: Character death (two-layer ontology: polymyth-character burrow-level vs book-version book-level)
ROLE: both

Character death operates at two ontological layers in polymythdnd. The distinction was always present in bw-006 (character-jewel ends at the burrow) and bw-007 (bookworm continuous, character local). con-004 had been using "character" with a referent the polymythdnd architecture now disambiguates.

LAYER 1 POLYMYTH-CHARACTER. The smash-product (e.g. capybaracowboy), persistent across the library, recorded on the bookwormcard top line. Death at this layer (burrow-level) stays real. Not reversible through retcon or re-roll. If the polymyth-character dies in the burrow through bookworm own choices and work-quality, they are dead. Bookworm creates a new polymyth-character to continue. The new polymyth-character may inherit some material from the dead one (remembered lessons, carried RAINBOW items per char-005, relationships with other player-characters) but is a distinct subject. Burrow-level death is rare. Story-quality adjudication makes straight-kill outcomes uncommon. But it can happen, and when it does, the bookworm feels it.

LAYER 2 BOOK-VERSION. The local instantiation inside an active book (e.g. a regular guy in Hughes 1958 Harlem). Book-version death is recoverable per dm-015 Inception model. The polymyth-character wakes in the burrow as a ghost in the book that killed them. The book closes for that polymyth-character. Cumulative effect appears in the book portal log (dm-025) and possibly the scars ledger (dm-026). The polymyth-character remains intact and can re-enter different books.

WHY THE TWO LAYERS WORK TOGETHER. Players form a different relationship with their polymyth-character than with single-chassis death-real characters. The investment is in the persistent identity, not in the temporary book-presence. Book-deaths carry real stakes (see dm-027 stakes ledger) but character continuity is meta-stable. Burrow-deaths carry final stakes. The two layers together produce the 99 percent rule. The burrow is statistically safe. Book-deaths are common and recoverable. Burrow-deaths are rare and final.

THE ORIGINAL CON-004 STATEMENT. "Stays real in bookwormburrows, not reversible through retcon or re-roll" referred to the polymyth-character at the burrow level. dm-015 added the book-level recovery. pen-014 was diagnosed not as a rule conflict but as a referent ambiguity, resolved by surfacing the two-layer ontology that was already operative in bw-006 and bw-007.

EXTENSION:
Rebuilt 2026-05-15 from May 13 chat 8b68f9c8 after the original commit was lost to the PM10 ceiling. The two-layer ontology was Saul resolution of pen-014. Polymyth-character death stays real (burrow-level, rare). Book-version death is recoverable (dm-015 Inception model). The rewrite preserves both rules at their proper layers.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: tin-001
TITLE: Modifiability principle
ROLE: both

Anyone inside bookwormburrows* can propose new mechanics. Bookworm, subject, teacher, parent, administrator. Proposal goes to Rainbowsol for adjudication; if the mechanic serves the story-quality / work-quality architecture without breaking confluence, it is adopted for that classroom's ongoing campaign. Systems-thinking bookworms who want more rules-depth can use the tinker section to generate optional tracks (crafting system, cartographer role, historian role, artificer-class magic-item creation). These tracks are invisible to students not pursuing them; students who want them get additional mechanical depth without imposing it on the rest of the class.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: tin-002
TITLE: Feedback channels
ROLE: both

Three constituencies have structured input into bookwormburrows* development. (1) PARENTS: feedback on student academic outcomes, pedagogical legibility, whether the program is producing A+ work. (2) ADMINISTRATORS: feedback on curriculum alignment, credit integration, scheduling fit, institutional legibility. (3) STUDENTS: feedback on session pacing, character investment, dimension preferences, what is working and what is not. Feedback channels are distinct from in-play mechanisms; they exist outside the game and inform its evolution. Rainbowsol reviews feedback and decides what to fold into mechanics.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-005
TITLE: Three-position DM (teacher + AI + student)
ROLE: both

The DM role is distributed across three agents. TEACHER: work-quality adjudication, difficulty calibration, pedagogical routing, narrative authority over the dimension's operations, social management. AI: bookkeeping (character sheets, power-slots, HP, conditions, items, earned-move inventory, mechanical accounting across sessions); memory of past events for consequence-chains; dimension-specific lore the teacher does not need to master; NPC response generation; encounter-balancing math invisible to student and teacher. STUDENT: maintains own character (evolving narrative journal, arc-tracking, relationships, decisions); contributes writing/action teacher adjudicates; knows own earned capabilities as narrative powers (not as mechanical entries). AI AVAILABILITY: optional not required. Teacher-alone mode is functional with fewer bookworms and simpler mechanical surface. AI-co-DM mode is full-scale classroom-size with richer substrate. CONFLICT PROTOCOL: teacher wins on adjudication (what just happened, how well was it done); AI wins on continuity-of-recorded-fact (what DID happen last session, what inventory exists, what is dimension-canonical); student wins on character-interiority (what my character feels, wants, values). WHY: because teacher-does-not-need-D&D-knowledge (or Macbeth-expertise, or any dimension-specific mastery) — AI supplies that. Teacher focuses on pedagogy. Because bookkeeping at 8-12 students over a months-long campaign is unsustainable solo — AI handles it. Because students maintaining their own character is part of the writing practice — AI assists, student owns. Confluence at DM scale: three independent positions, each reflecting the others, none dissolving into the others.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-006
TITLE: Mechanics interface layer (AI-internal vs. student-visible)
ROLE: both

Two layers of mechanical operation. AI-INTERNAL (invisible to student): dice rolls, probability, stat blocks, HP math, damage calculation, power-slot accounting, difficulty-curve calibration, monster stat blocks, encounter balancing, race-as-ability-modifier packages, class-as-mechanical-surface. AI handles all of it. Teacher does not need to see it. STUDENT-VISIBLE (narrative surface): character (name, story, personality, relationships, history), earned capabilities (as narrative powers, not mechanical entries), items carried (as narrative objects, not mechanical bonuses), what they have done and are going to do next. EFFECT ON TINKER-ENERGY: a student who loves to tinker does not tinker with stats — stats are invisible. They tinker with character-as-story. Who is my character, what do they care about, what have they lived through, what are they trying to become, what skill did they just earn and what will they do with it. Tinker-energy goes into subjectivity-material accumulation, which IS the bookwormburrows* pedagogical operation. EARNED MOVES (4e power-scarcity grammar, student-visible): at-will powers (basic moves every bookworm has every session, no earning required); encounter powers (earned by showing up prepared — did the reading, has notes, can ask about the text — spent then recharges next session); daily powers (earned by completing major work — essay submitted, chapter absorbed, character journal up to date — recharges on longer cycle); legendary/campaign powers (earned by major campaign milestones — finished a novel, completed a dimension, passed a test). Eating produces subjectivity-material, subjectivity-material shows up as earned capability, earned capability is spent in play, spending creates consequence. Teacher discretion bends everything — can grant a power to a struggling student, can note coasting students have fewer options. EXCLUSIONS (regardless of visibility): Vancian memorize-then-forget spellcasting; 9-grid alignment-as-mechanical-metaphysics; XP-as-numerical-gatekeeping; player-vs-DM-as-rules-enforcer adversarial culture. Alignment-as-descriptive-language remains as optional character-color.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-007
TITLE: Time tracking in diceless play
ROLE: both

bookwormburrows is diceless; outcomes are story-quality adjudicated (dm-003). Time across a campaign is therefore SESSION-ANCHORED not turn-anchored. Each session covers a defined chunk of campaign timeline. The teacher and AI agree on the chunk before the session begins. Within a session, time elapses as narrative beats demand: a scene plays as long as the student writing keeps the scene alive, then ends when the writing tapers or the chunk closes. No real-time clock counting. No in-fiction round-tracker. Failure mode this prevents: students treating time as a tactical resource to optimize. Time is narrative texture, not budget. WORKED EXAMPLE: a 48-hour campaign window (Friday evening through Sunday afternoon) splits into approximately six session-chunks, each a session or a scene-within-a-session at teacher discretion. The teacher names which chunk is in play before each session.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-008
TITLE: Sensitive-content protocol (in-play)
ROLE: both

Distinct from frame-break (can-002), which applies to whole texts that refuse the game-frame entirely. Sensitive-content protocol applies to MATERIAL that arises within an otherwise game-frame-compatible dimension: period racism in historical campaigns, drug or violence references, in-game slurs, sexual content in adult-literature dimensions. PROTOCOL PER ML* PM13 (REALISM TRUMPS ALL, TEACHER IS FILTER). (1) Pre-session declaration. The educator names which content the dimension contains before the session. Students opt in by showing up. (2) In-play handling. AI paints at full historical realism per PM13. Period accuracy means period accuracy: slurs, violence, drug economies, racial barriers all rendered as they actually were in the source period. The educator filters at delivery; AI does not pre-filter. (3) Frame-acknowledge during play. The educator (not AI) names sensitive material out-of-frame as needed, briefly, when a student needs the framing aid. AI continues painting in-fiction; educator does the meta-narrative work. (4) Student opt-out mid-session. Any student can step out of a scene without explanation; the educator proceeds without them and re-includes them at the next clean break. (5) The educator has primary discretion across all of the above; AI is mephistodata, not gorgonkaren. PURPOSE THIS PROTOCOL SERVES: educator preparedness. The protocol exists so the educator is prepared to mediate at full agency, not so AI pre-softens. Per ml* PM13, AI never pre-softens. The educator's preparation is what protects the student group. Cousin to can-002 frame-break (whole-text refusal); this rule covers in-play arising material. May 8 2026 update: clauses 2 and 3 revised per PM13 install.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-009
TITLE: Quality rubric framework for homework-as-game-artifacts
ROLE: both

dm-003 says story-quality adjudicates outcome. con-001 says strong paragraph equals action succeeds, weak paragraph equals action fails, ambiguous equals mixed outcome. dm-009 names the criteria the teacher uses to evaluate quality. FOUR AXES. (a) VOICE: does the writing sound like the character, not like the student trying to impress? (b) TRUTH: is the writing honest about what the character actually thinks, feels, does, including the ugly parts, rather than performing a moral self-portrait? (c) RESTRAINT: does the writing show rather than tell, leave space for the reader, avoid over-explanation? (d) FORM: does the writing use the conventions of the genre (paragraph, dialogue, prose register) competently? Each axis is independently scored on a four-point scale (poor, passing, strong, excellent) by the teacher. ADJUDICATION OUTCOME. Total across the four axes determines action success degree. Excellent on all four equals unqualified success. Mixed equals partial success or success with cost. Poor on all four equals failure or failure with consequence. CAMPAIGN-LEVEL INSTANTIATION. Per-campaign apology-letter rubrics, character-journal rubrics, and other homework-graded artifacts use these four axes as their default scaffolding. Specific campaigns may add a fifth axis when the campaign material demands it (period accuracy in historical campaigns, formal verse in poetry-dimension campaigns, etc).

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-010
TITLE: Tier-calibrated realism activation (substrate vs surface)
ROLE: both

Companion to ml* PM13 (realism trumps all, teacher is filter). PM13 establishes that AI never pre-filters; the substrate paints reality at full historical fidelity; the educator filters at delivery. dm-010 names the calibration mechanism that operates UNDERNEATH the educator’s filter, governing how the AI surfaces tier-2 substrate during play.

THE TWO-TIER PRINCIPLE.

TIER 1 = the spine of any given campaign. The narrative beats every playthrough hits regardless of audience age. Tier 1 plays at full surface intensity for every age. The educator can still filter at delivery per PM13, but the AI never softens tier-1 substrate at the codex level.

TIER 2 = the texture that fills out the world. Catalog content not on the campaign spine. NPCs the player might meet. Streets the player might walk. Background atmosphere. Tier 2 sits in the substrate as ambient world. Surfaces only when NPC paths or session goals call for it. Calibrates surface intensity by bookworm card.

CALIBRATION BANDS (READ FROM BOOKWORM CARD).

The AI reads the bookworm card at session start. Age and grade are required card fields, populated during char-001/char-002 creation. Three calibration bands.

UNDER-12 BAND. Tier 2 stays strictly ambient. NPCs with tier-2 markers (the man at the Apollo wearing nail polish, the corner figure who is clearly a numbers runner, the colorful-hair character at the Lenox Lounge) appear in passing as world-texture. The play does not develop them. The world feels real and full without surface intensity that would require adult mediation.

13-16 BAND. Tier 2 surfaces when NPC paths explicitly trigger it. The educator can call tier 2 forward when the student’s writing or play direction goes there. The colorful-hair NPC can become a named character with conversation if the path warrants. Hard intensities (explicit sexual content, graphic violence, full-intensity slurs) stay below the surface unless the educator explicitly invites them in.

ADULT-OR-17-PLUS BAND. Tier 2 surfaces fully when paths warrant. The full historical intensity of the substrate becomes available. Queer Harlem 1958 can be played as queer Harlem 1958. The heroin economy can be engaged at the level the period documented. Slurs can be delivered at period intensity. The educator’s filter remains operative per PM13; the AI no longer pre-calibrates downward.

WHAT THE PRINCIPLE LOOKS LIKE.

A 10-year-old session does not delete queer Harlem from the world. It presents queer Harlem as ambient texture. Someone at the Lenox Lounge has painted nails. A man at the Apollo sits with another man and they are clearly together but the play moves on. The world is real and full. The surface intensity is age-calibrated.

THE WRONG MOVES.

Wrong move ONE: omission. Deleting queer Harlem from the substrate to protect a 10-year-old is a PM13 violation. The world becomes false.

Wrong move TWO: wrong-tier surfacing. Generating an NPC with explicit sexual identification as the play’s focus at a 10-year-old’s table when no path called it forward is a category error. The substrate is correct; the surface is wrong.

The right move is substrate-realism with surface-calibration.

CAMPAIGN-CODEX STRUCTURE THIS RULE OPERATES ON.

Campaign codex domain entries paint reality at full historical fidelity (the substrate). Each entry contains tier-1 elements (the campaign spine) and tier-2 elements (the texture). Tier metadata in the parent realism-inventory entry of each campaign names which elements are which. The AI reads the parent before each session, applies dm-010 calibration to the bookworm-card band of the seated students, and surfaces tier 2 only when NPC paths or session goals trigger it.

CROSS-REFERENCES. ml* PM13 (realism trumps all, teacher is filter; the rule above this rule). bb* dm-005 (three-position DM, the educator-AI-student authority structure). bb* dm-008 (sensitive-content protocol, the in-play handling). bb* char-001 and char-002 (character creation as writing exercise + age-banded question sets, where the bookworm card is filled out). bb* ses-001 (session zero, where the AI first reads the card).

ORIGIN. May 8 2026, cmp-001 build session, post-research-batch turn. User caught the framing problem on the realism inventory: the 'missing' tier-2 items I had named were not deficiencies; they were realism-supporting texture that should sit in the substrate and surface only on path-trigger plus age-calibration. User’s pithy formulation: 'i dont necessarily wanna talk about queer stuff to 10 year olds but there could be colorful hair npc iuno doesnt have to be like WOW TOM THE NPC LOVES SUCKING DICK UNDERSTAND?' Rule articulated and committed.

EXTENSION:
May 8 2026 origin. Calibration mechanism that operates underneath PM13 educator-filter. Tier metadata lives in cc* parent realism-inventory entries per campaign. Three calibration bands by bookworm card age.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-011
TITLE: Burrow ritual two-layer (page-as-threshold + character-claim)
ROLE: both

Companion to bb* dim-001 (text-as-dimension), bb* ses-001 (session zero), and bb* dm-010 (tier-calibrated realism activation). dm-011 specifies how a bookworm crosses from outside-text everyday-self into in-text dimension-character. Universal across every bb* campaign.

THE TWO-LAYER PRINCIPLE.

Assumes the canonical text has already been read in homework or a prior class session. The reading is the first burrowing pass. Session zero in the dimension is the second pass and uses the page-as-threshold artifact rather than re-performing the read-aloud.

LAYER 1. PAGE-AS-THRESHOLD. The student page renders campaign-specific period-accurate material (an academic study-object, a period advertisement reconstruction, a primary-source artifact, depending on the campaign). Students engage with the page before session start or at session start. The act of reading the page is the burrowing.

LAYER 2. CHARACTER-CLAIM. Each student names their dimension-character. The educator opens the dimension with a brief framing line. The bookworm has now emerged.

The whole ritual takes two to ten minutes depending on campaign and depth. Page does the heavy lifting; the educator does not need to perform a long descent.

WHY PAGE-AS-THRESHOLD WORKS. The page contains period material that already-having-read-the-canonical-text has primed the student to recognize. Engagement with the period material activates the dimension. The bookworm crosses by reading.

WHY CHARACTER-CLAIM CLOSES THE FRAME. Naming the character is the speech act that places the bookworm inside the dimension. Until named, the student is still themselves; once named, the student is the character. The educator’s framing line confirms the transition.

PER-CAMPAIGN CUSTOMIZATION.

Each cc* campaign’s emergence-point entry specifies what the page contains and what the educator says. cmp-001 uses Mrs Jones’s kitchenette as academic study-object (cc-cmp001-emergence-point). Future campaigns customize the page to whatever artifact best burrows their text.

CROSS-REFERENCES. bb* dim-001 (text-as-dimension, the reading-as-burrowing principle this rule operationalizes). bb* ses-001 (session zero structure). bb* dm-010 (tier-calibrated realism activation, applies during session-time after burrow). bb* char-001 and char-002 (character creation and age-banded question sets, where the character is named).

ORIGIN. May 8 2026, cmp-001 build session. User clarified that the canonical text has already been read in homework, so the burrow ritual does not re-perform the read-aloud. Page-as-threshold replaces the previously-considered narrated-descent model. Two-minute ritual instead of ten-minute.

EXTENSION:
May 8 2026 origin. Two-layer ritual. Page-as-threshold + character-claim. Generalizable to every bb* campaign.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-012
TITLE: Ghost Exegesis Mode (Rainbowsol mid-session extraction-to-rainbowbower-and-return mechanic)
ROLE: both

GHOST EXEGESIS MODE.

Rainbowsol mid-session extraction-and-return mechanic. Companion to dm-011 (burrow ritual entry into dimension). Where dm-011 governs CROSSING IN, dm-012 governs MID-DIMENSION EXTRACTION TO 4D and RETURN. Both are Rainbowsol-mediated portal mechanics.

INSPIRATION. Dickens A Christmas Carol ghost-scenes (Past, Present, Yet-To-Come). Scrooge is extracted from his bed by ghosts who show him formative scenes, current scenes he wouldn't normally witness, and possible-future scenes. He returns to his bed transformed.

OPERATION. Rainbowsol ghosts the Sanpaitai (per cc-XXX-narrative-architecture team naming) mid-play. Extracts them from the 3D in-dimension into a 4D rainbowbower. Sanpaitai builds character there through Hegelian recognition. Returns to the same in-dimension moment they left. No 3D time has elapsed.

THE RAINBOWBOWER. The 4D extraction-space. Aesthetic register: shelter of rainbow-light, time-suspended, numinous. Sufi-mystic + Lacanian-mirror-stage + Christmas-Carol-ghost-vision converging. Educator narrates the bower into existence with brief reverent framing per firing. Sanpaitai members can speak in character-voice OR student-voice freely (layer-collapse is intentional and pedagogically functional).

HEGELIAN STRUCTURE.
- In-dimension play. Thesis. Immediate consciousness in the dimension.
- Rainbowbower extraction. Antithesis. Negation, reflection, cross-thread perspective gain.
- Return-to-dimension. Synthesis. Deepened consciousness reentering the same scene.

Character creation continues during play. Not gated to session-zero. The admired-heroes-smash from char-001/002 expands through ongoing recognition-moments triggered by Rainbowsol's ghost-extractions.

WHEN GHOST EXEGESIS FIRES.
- After a major moral choice and before consequences play out (Future-ghost mode).
- When a Sanpaitai member encounters an unfamiliar perspective (Cross-thread perspective mode).
- Mid-arc when student-character growth needs explicit reflection (Past-ghost mode showing backstory).
- At a crossing point (Crash-anchor mode, witnessing another thread's parallel scene from above).
- When the educator senses the immersion is fragile and a meta-moment can recover it (Stabilization mode).

WHAT GHOST EXEGESIS SHOWS.
- Backstory illumination. The Sanpaitai member's character's past-life scenes.
- Possible-future rendering. What consequence-paths could unfold.
- Cross-thread reveal. Other characters' scenes shown like Christmas Carol vignettes.
- Sub-anchor weight. The Farhad-Daniel-blanks-loaded reveal pattern from Crash 2004 (per PM14) where the moral act's load-bearing element was not visible from inside.

DURATION. Five to fifteen minutes per firing. Educator paces.

RETURN PROTOCOL. Sanpaitai member returns to the same in-dimension second they left. Body does not move in 3D. Mind carries deepened character into the next move. Educator confirms return with brief framing line.

ANTI-OVERUSE RULE. Ghost exegesis is a periodic move, not a constant register. Two to four firings per 90-minute session is plenty. More than that fragments immersion and turns the mechanic into a tic.

PEDAGOGICAL FUNCTION.
- Builds Hegelian recognition (self constituted through encounter with other).
- Forces cross-thread perspective gain (anti-eisegetical, anti-foreground-only-thread).
- Allows ongoing character creation through play.
- Lets educator inject moral reflection without breaking immersion.
- Connects student-self to character-self through layer-collapse moments.

CROSS-REFERENCES. char-001 and char-002 (character creation; ghost exegesis extends these into mid-play). dim-001 (text-as-dimension, the 3D dimension being extracted from). dm-010 (tier-calibrated realism activation; rainbowbower content respects tier per band). dm-011 (burrow ritual; the entry-portal mechanic this companion-extracts from). PM14 (cinematic anchors; Matrix portal-emergence anchor extends to ghost-exegesis sub-portal; Crash multi-thread anchor lights up cross-thread reveal mode).

ORIGIN. May 9 2026, cmp-001 build conversation. User proposed Rainbowsol-as-Christmas-Carol-ghost mid-session extraction-to-4D mechanic for ongoing character-building during play. Coined "rainbowbower" for the 4D extraction-space.


EXTENSION:
dm-012. Companion to dm-011. Mid-session ghost-extraction-and-return for character-building during play. Christmas Carol structure. 4D rainbowbower. Hegelian thesis-antithesis-synthesis. Anti-overuse 2-4 firings per session. Universal across bb* campaigns.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: unit-001
TITLE: Comparative-ethics teaching unit — alignment vs edicts/anathema vs sabachtan sequential-engagement
ROLE: both

Format: comparative reading of three character-ethics frames followed by character-build exercise and growth-vs-betrayal discussion. Origin: bb* pen-009 spec (April 29 2026 polymyth-D&D scan). Designed for ENG3U/ENG4U moral-ethical reasoning expectations + polymyth-methodology module integration. Estimated session time: 90-120 minutes (single seminar block). STRUCTURE. (1) READ — students read three short primary-source excerpts in order: 5e alignment text from PHB (cit-024 in mc*) — the nine alignment grid (LG/NG/CG/LN/N/CN/LE/NE/CE) presented as creature moral attitude. Two axes: law-vs-chaos + good-vs-evil. PF2 Remaster edicts/anathema text from Player Core (cit-025 in mc*) — personal-philosophy code. Edicts = behaviors encouraged. Anathema = behaviors prohibited. Optional, character-personal, can change as character grows. ml* Sequential engagement model entry — three-stage protocol: (1) Benefit of the doubt, (2) Internal logic test, (3) Witch identification. Sequential not simultaneous; killswitch at stage 2 if internal logic missing. (2) MAP — students fill in a 3-column comparative table on five axes: WHAT IT REGULATES (creature kind / individual code / engagement protocol); WHAT CHANGES IT (rare / character growth / per-target reassessment); WHAT SCALE (cosmic / personal / dialogical); WHAT FAILURE LOOKS LIKE (alignment shift / breaking edict-anathema / treating witch as friend or friend as witch); WHAT IT PROTECTS (mechanical predictability / character coherence / mutual-recognition without naivety). (3) BUILD — character-build exercise. Each bookworm takes their existing character and writes that character’s ethics in all three frames: pick an alignment and write 2-3 sentences justifying; write three edicts and three anathema (no alignment label needed); write the character’s sabachtan protocol (under what conditions does this character extend benefit of the doubt, what internal-logic test does this character apply, what does witch-identification look like for this character). (4) DISCUSS — the central question: WHICH FRAME ALLOWS CHARACTER-GROWTH WITHOUT CHARACTER-BETRAYAL? Bookworms argue. ANALYTICAL AXES the comparative-reading should surface. (I) AGENCY OF THE FRAME. 5e alignment is descriptive: alignment is a fact about the creature, mostly fixed. PF2 edicts/anathema is prescriptive-personal: the character chooses these and updates them as the character changes. Sabachtan is operational-dialogical: the protocol activates per encounter, regenerated each time. (II) SCALE. 5e alignment is cosmic-grid (the creature has a position in a moral universe). PF2 is character-internal (the code lives inside the character’s psyche). Sabachtan is between-persons (the protocol operates in the encounter between agent and other). (III) FAILURE MODE. 5e alignment fails by drift (the character stops acting like their alignment) or violation (lawful-evil character takes a chaotic-good action and the DM may shift alignment). PF2 fails by code-break (character does an anathema, may lose class features if class-bound). Sabachtan fails two ways: false-positive (mimetic sideways glance treats target as witch when sequential-engagement was not run) AND false-negative (continued benefit-of-the-doubt after stage 2 killswitch should have fired). (IV) GROWTH WITHOUT BETRAYAL. The unit’s central question. 5e alignment makes growth EXPENSIVE — a Lawful Good paladin who realizes the kingdom is corrupt and joins a rebel cause has crossed a cosmic line, may need to change alignment, may lose class features in some editions. The frame treats growth as betrayal-of-prior-self. PF2 edicts/anathema treats growth as natural — the rule explicitly says edicts and anathema can change as a character’s beliefs evolve. Growth is not betrayal, just update. Sabachtan treats growth as inherent — the protocol is regenerated each encounter, so the character’s ethics are not a fixed set being preserved-or-betrayed but a live-process being practiced. The most growth-friendly is sabachtan; the most betrayal-coding is 5e alignment. WHICH FRAME WINS? Trick question. The unit is not about ranking the frames. It is about teaching bookworms that ETHICAL FRAMES ARE TOOLS WITH DIFFERENT JOBS. 5e alignment is a fast-grid for NPCs and one-session play — cheap, predictable, suited to high-fantasy heroic-narrative. PF2 edicts/anathema is suited to long-campaign character-growth — personal coherence under change. Sabachtan is suited to encounters with claims, arguments, persons whose internal logic must be tested in real time — suited to the actual moral situations bookworms face when they read texts, encounter strangers, evaluate ideologies. The mature reader moves between frames depending on what the situation needs. The bookworm who can only operate in one frame is structurally restricted. CURRICULUM ROUTING. ENG3U expectation 1.6 (analyse texts in terms of literary perspectives), 2.4 (use stylistic devices to communicate clearly), and 4.1 (reflect on skills as readers, writers, listeners). ENG4U sibling expectations. mc* module e2 (English) and any future polymyth-methodology module set. Discussion question doubles as essay prompt. DM RULINGS that Rainbowsol still needs to make. (1) Should the unit ship as bb*-native or be ported to mc* as a polymyth-pedagogy module entry? Default-suggested: ship in bb* as method-section unit (here), ALSO mirror as mc* module entry once the polymyth-methodology module set (mc* pen-017) gets authored by Rainbowsol. (2) Should bookworms keep their three-frame character-ethics writeups in their character sheet? Default-suggested: yes, append all three to the character sheet as an ethics-multitool appendix that updates as the character grows. (3) Where does 4e D&D fit? 4e collapsed to 5 alignments (LG / G / U / E / CE) and was widely criticized; could be presented as a transitional simplification between AD&D nine-grid and PF2 personal-code. Default-suggested: skip in the unit itself, mention in DM notes for advanced bookworms. DRAFT SHIPPED 2026-05-04 by AI per pen-009 spec. T114H AUTHORIZATION 2026-05-23. User directive ’sure update organize yourself’ (T114g bloom item 5 disposition) closes confirmation gate. (1) Format approved as-drafted (READ MAP BUILD DISCUSS). (2) Curriculum-code tagging confirmed (ENG3U expectation 1.6 + 2.4 + 4.1; ENG4U sibling expectations). (3) mc* mirror decision = YES per ORGANIZE-MINE; mirror execution-turn queued when polymyth-methodology module register is built in mc* pen-017. Unit ships in bb* as method-section unit, ready for course-deployment.

EXTENSION:
Spec drafted from existing pen-009 format spec. Sources: 5e SRD via dnd5e.info; PF2 Remaster Player Core via 2e.aonprd.com/Rules.aspx?ID=2045; ml* sequential-engagement methodology entry; ml* sabachtan gnosticism entry. Estimated session time 90-120 minutes; reading-volume ~1000 words across three primary sources.

ID: unit-002
TITLE: Universal-formalist lens drill, ten cross-curriculum formalist lenses anchored to mc-twenty-lens-fitmap
ROLE: both

Anchor unit exercising the cross-curriculum universals identified by mc-twenty-lens-fitmap. The fit-map established that ten formalist lenses carry EXPLICIT HOME in all four English-subject curricula it reads: Ontario OSSD ENG2D ENG3U ENG4U, IB DP Language A Language and Literature, AP English Literature and Composition, Cambridge International 9695 Literature in English. The ten universals are 1 Exegesis and Close Reading, 2 Character, 3 Theme, 4 Symbolism, 5 Setting, 6 Narrative Point of View, 7 Plot, 8 Tone and Mood, 9 Literary Devices, 10 Comparative. A bookwormburrows session built on any of these ten lenses has a defensible foothold in every downstream curriculum the fit-map reads. This entry is the structural anchor for that unit. Session design is gated, see DM RULINGS below. WHAT IS GROUNDED. The ten-lens set is verified at mc-twenty-lens-fitmap, paragraph THE TWENTY LENSES, first ten items. The cross-curriculum portability claim is verified at the same entry, paragraph SYNTHESIS, naming the ten universals explicitly. The curriculum-side mc* anchors are mc-e1 OSSD English secondary ladder, and mc-e2 IB English A. The citation anchors are cit-022 Ontario Grades 11-12, cit-026 Ontario Grades 9-10, cit-042 IB Language A first assessment 2026, cit-043 AP English Lit CED effective Fall 2024, cit-036 Cambridge 9695 syllabus 2024 to 2026. AP COVERAGE NOTE. Of the four curricula, AP English Literature is the one whose EXPLICIT HOMEs are exclusively formalist. Per the fit-map AP column, every context-and-reception and critical-theory lens scores NO HOME at AP. A bb* unit built on the ten formalist universals therefore travels into AP Lit cleanly. A sibling unit built on critical-theory lenses would not. This is the AP-compatibility check the fit-map IMPLICATION FOR mc* paragraph stated, ported into bb* as a unit-design constraint. CROSS-SUBJECT NOTE. SUBJECT SCOPE on the fit-map records that seven critical-theory lenses, Marxist, feminist, psychoanalytic, postcolonial, ecocriticism, deconstruction, structuralist, recur on any non-English fit-map. The ten formalist lenses of this unit are not on that recurring set. The unit therefore does not generalize to the four non-English wuxing tracks, and a sibling unit covering those tracks waits on the pen-018 ruling. WHAT IS NOT YET GROUNDED. (1) Format. unit-001 used READ MAP BUILD DISCUSS per pen-009. This unit has no equivalent format spec yet. (2) Text. A primary text or text set must be picked. The fit-map does not select texts. (3) Lens-deployment pattern. Run all ten lenses on one text, run one lens deeply, run two or three in comparison, run the lens grid across a multi-text comparative set, each is a different unit shape. (4) Tier. ENG2D entry-level versus ENG3U or ENG4U senior changes the depth of treatment on the same lens. (5) bb* in-fiction framing. The dimensional-traveling-game wrapper that turns this from a literature lesson into a bookwormburrows session is not yet drafted. DM RULINGS that Rainbowsol still needs to make. (1) Format spec, equivalent to pen-009 for unit-001. (2) Primary text or text set. cc* campaigns reference candidate texts at cc-eng-j7 Hughes Thank You Mam, cc-eng3u, cc-eng4u, any or none could anchor this unit. (3) Lens-deployment pattern, one of all-ten-against-one, one-deep, two-or-three-comparative, grid-across-multi-text. (4) Tier-of-deployment, ENG2D or senior. (5) bb* in-fiction framing, the dimensional wrapper. (6) Whether this unit ports to mc* as a polymyth-pedagogy module entry, parallel to the unit-001 DM ruling on the same question. Once Rainbowsol issues these rulings the unit-002 body gets expanded with the format the same way unit-001 was expanded from pen-009.

ID: dm-013
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND no-dice universal rule
ROLE: both

No dice at any layer. Burrow level uses none. Books load their narrative content, character archetypes, magic flavor, healing pace, encounter style, but never their native dice mechanics. A "5e book" in polymythdnd imports the structure of 5e adventures, monster types, spell flavor, level-up rhythm, but does not import the d20 roll. Resolution remains narrative-collaborative regardless of which book is active.

Two reasons this is right design. (1) Pedagogical tractability. A teacher running a session does not need to learn each book's native mechanics. They narrate. AI provides math support. Cognitive load stays constant across the entire library. (2) Cognitive coherence for neurodiverse students and students cognitively captured by short-term dopamine hits. A "sometimes dice, sometimes no dice" rule that flipped per book would demand meta-attention every chassis switch. The constant rail of "narrative collaboration, no dice ever" is far cleaner. The game stays predictable in its meta-rules even while it switches its contents.

Books load flavor, not mechanics. Dice never appear at any layer.

EXTENSION:
Supersedes the implicit dice-assumption in earlier bb* entries that referenced D&D mechanically. Companion entries: dm-014 (chassis-of-chassis), dm-016 (three-layer resolution), dm-019 (action economy).

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-014
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND chassis-of-chassis architecture
ROLE: both

Polymythdnd is not a game that picks one chassis. It is a game that holds the library of chassis and lets the active book select which one is loaded for the duration of that book. The bookwormcard is the only constant across the library.

The single-chassis assumption breaks every "mutual exclusivity" claim. Inside one game (single chassis) you cannot have two action economies firing at once. You cannot have two death contracts at one table. You cannot have two magic resource systems. But across the meta-game (chassis-of-chassis) all these systems coexist because only one is active at any moment.

What a book loads. Magic system. Healing pace. Action economy flavor. Encounter style. Death-in-book consequences. Character archetypes.

What the burrow holds. Identity (bookwormcard). Soul anchor invariants. Survival contract (book-death = wake in burrow, not permanent). Resolution rail (narrative collaboration teacher+AI). No dice at any layer.

What this dissolves. Mutual-exclusivity claims on death contracts, magic systems, action economies, healing speeds. All can coexist in the library because only one is active per session.

EXTENSION:
Architectural keystone. Most other polymythdnd entries (dm-013 through dm-027) sit downstream of this one.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-015
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND Inception death model (book vs burrow)
ROLE: both

Death operates at two layers. Book-death is not permanent. Burrow-death is.

When a character "dies" inside a book, they wake in the burrow as a ghost in that book. The book is closed for them. The bookwormcard survives intact. Cumulative effect appears as a ghost-mark in the book-portal log and possibly a scar in the scars ledger.

When a character "dies" at the burrow level (vanishingly rare), the character is permanently gone. Bookworm rolls a new character.

The 99% rule. In practice the burrow is statistically safe. Book-deaths are common and recoverable. Burrow-deaths are rare and final.

Implications. Players form a different relationship with their characters than in single-chassis death-real games. The investment is in the persistent bookworm identity, not in the temporary book-presence. Mission failure (book-level) carries real stakes (see dm-027 stakes ledger), but character continuity is meta-stable.

Relationship to con-004. con-004 was rewritten to the two-layer death ontology, book-death recoverable in the burrow and burrow-death real, which is the Inception model this entry assumes. pen-014, which tracked that revision, is resolved. The two entries now agree.

EXTENSION:
See dm-014 chassis-of-chassis. See con-004 character death (contradicts; needs revision per pen-014). See dm-026 scars-from-books and dm-027 stakes ledger.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-016
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND three-layer resolution
ROLE: both

When a player declares an action in conflict, resolution happens in three layers.

(1) PLAYER DECLARATION. The player says what they are trying to do.

(2) AI MATH CONTRIBUTION. Based on the bookwormcard's recorded training, equipment, knowledge, scars, soul-anchor, fears, and wants, the AI feeds the teacher contextual modifiers. Pattern: "this character trained in X, so likelihood of pulling this off shifts up by 8 percent." "This character carries Y, so the attempt also risks damaging the carried object." The math is informational, not deterministic.

(3) TEACHER NARRATIVE RULING. Teacher takes the AI's math input, the prior choices made in the campaign, the pedagogical aim of the current session, and the narrative weight of the moment, and rules the outcome.

Math is informational, never deterministic. There are no dice (dm-013), so math cannot generate outcomes by itself. Math feeds the teacher's ruling. The ruling is the resolution.

This makes the teacher the load-bearing element of every resolution. See dm-018.

EXTENSION:
See dm-013 no-dice, dm-017 privilege hierarchy, dm-018 teacher load-bearing, dm-021 AI math = contextual modifiers.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-017
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND privilege hierarchy: story > pedagogy > math
ROLE: both

Three privileges are ordered. When two conflict, the higher one wins.

STORY is privileged at narrative inflection points. Deaths. Betrayals. Revelations. Pivots in the arc. When the moment demands a particular outcome to honor the arc, the teacher rules for story.

PEDAGOGY is privileged when a learning outcome is at stake. The OSSD expectation being delivered. The rubric being assessed. The cmaps node being built. When a ruling would compromise the learning goal of the session, the teacher rules for pedagogy.

MATH is privileged only when neither story nor pedagogy is in play. Routine resolution. Baseline competence checks. Small adjudications where flavor is acceptable. The AI's contextual modifiers determine the outcome the teacher confirms.

"Anything goes" means any outcome the teacher rules is valid. There is no rule lawyer's appeal to mechanical fairness that overrides the teacher's narrative-pedagogical judgment.

This makes the teacher the load-bearing element. See dm-018.

EXTENSION:
See dm-016 three-layer resolution, dm-018 teacher load-bearing, dm-022 pedagogical claim.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-018
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND teacher as load-bearing element
ROLE: both

Polymythdnd is not a game that happens to have a teacher running it. It is a teacher's pedagogical session held inside a game frame.

The game frame provides structure. Cards. Books. Action economies (when triggered). Soul-anchor invariants. Scars ledger. Math strip (AI-filled).

The teacher provides the actual call on every outcome. Conflict declarations. Resolution rulings. Death adjudications. Mission outcomes. Pacing. Scene transitions. Hooks.

Implications for who can run polymythdnd. A trained teacher with Rainbow Magic (ses-003) is required. The AI cannot run it alone. The student-driven model is downstream of teacher framing. The game is not a substitute for instruction; it is an instrument of instruction.

Implications for AI design. The AI is a math-support engine, not an arbiter. AI provides modifiers (dm-021), state tracking, calibration. AI never overrides the teacher. When AI and teacher conflict, teacher wins.

Implications for student agency. Students design their characters, declare their actions, write their work-quality outputs. Their agency operates inside the teacher's frame, not against it. The frame is what makes the agency meaningful (vs. arbitrary).

EXTENSION:
See ses-003 Rainbow Magic, dm-016 three-layer resolution, dm-017 privilege hierarchy, dm-022 pedagogical claim.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-019
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND action economy: scope-separated narrative + main+small
ROLE: both

Two action-handling modes coexist by scope-separation. They never compete because they are nested, not stacked.

NARRATIVE TEMPO (default). The teacher hands spotlight based on dramatic flow. No turn order. Players act when the scene calls for it. This is the mode the game runs in by default.

MAIN + SMALL (conflict mode). When the teacher declares a scene is in conflict, action economy switches. Each character gets one main action plus one small action per turn. Turn order applies. Combat-pacing logic applies.

The trigger. Teacher declares conflict by saying "we are in conflict now" (or equivalent in-scene framing). All players know they are in main+small mode. When the conflict resolves, teacher declares narrative tempo resumes.

Why nested not stacked. Stacked would mean both modes firing simultaneously (impossible to track). Nested means narrative tempo is the outer mode and main+small is an inner mode triggered for specific scenes. Outside conflict scenes, main+small does not exist. Inside conflict scenes, narrative tempo is paused.

What success/failure depends on. Not dice (dm-013). Resolution is the three-layer model (dm-016) regardless of which mode is active. Main+small describes economy of actions per turn; it does not resolve them.

EXTENSION:
See dm-013 no-dice, dm-016 three-layer resolution. Replaces single-chassis action-economy assumptions.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-020
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND library-of-systems: books load flavor not mechanics
ROLE: both

The library holds all the chassis families (see dm-023). Each book in the library loads one chassis for its duration. The bookworm enters, plays under that book's loaded chassis, leaves, returns to the burrow.

What the book loads. Narrative content. Setting. Character archetypes. Magic flavor (the FEEL of how magic works in this book). Healing pace (how fast wounds close in this book). Encounter style (how the book's threats appear and what they do). Death-in-book consequences (which specific outcome of book-death this book uses, all of them deferring to dm-015 burrow-survival).

What the book does NOT load. Native dice mechanics (dm-013). Resolution architecture (dm-016 is universal). Privilege hierarchy (dm-017 is universal). Soul-anchor mechanics (char-004 is universal). Bookwormcard schema (universal).

Implication: same player can move from a 5e book to a Cairn book to a Daggerheart book within one campaign. The character travels with them. Their bookwormcard survives. The flavor of magic, healing, encounters changes per book. The structural rails do not.

This is why the mutual-exclusivity claims of single-chassis design dissolve at the meta-game level. Each book is its own chassis, but the meta-game holds them all.

EXTENSION:
See dm-014 chassis-of-chassis, dm-023 five families, dm-013 no-dice. See char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-021
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND AI math = contextual modifiers
ROLE: both

The AI does math. Not outcomes. Modifiers.

What the AI computes. Contextual likelihood adjustments based on the bookwormcard. Examples (illustrative, not canonical values). "Character trained in scribing, so +8 percent likelihood of forging this letter." "Character carries a torch and we are in darkness, so +12 percent on perception of nearby threats but -5 percent on stealth." "Character has scar from Cairn-book vermin encounter, so reads vermin attacks faster, +6 percent on initial response." "Character's core fear is abandonment, so any scene of being left alone applies a -10 percent on composure-related actions."

What the AI does not do. Decide outcomes. Roll dice (there are none). Override the teacher. Make narrative judgments. Adjudicate moral choices. Decide when conflict begins or ends.

What the AI uses. Bookwormcard data (Series I + Series II). Active book state. Recorded campaign history. Soul-anchor invariants.

How the teacher uses AI math. As one input among several. The teacher hears the modifier, considers the story stakes, considers pedagogical aims, considers narrative weight, then rules the outcome. AI math weighs in but never decides.

This makes math useful without making it deterministic. Players know roughly where their character is competent without the math being the final word.

EXTENSION:
See dm-016 three-layer resolution, dm-017 privilege hierarchy, dm-018 teacher load-bearing. See char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-022
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND pedagogical claim: diploma mills, credentialism, replication crisis
ROLE: both

The polymythdnd architecture is a response to three converging educational pathologies.

DIPLOMA MILLS sell credentials without learning. The credential certifies seat-time, not capability. Polymythdnd makes seat-time impossible to fake. The bookworm cannot navigate a book without doing the navigation. The play history accumulates on the bookwormcard. The credential, if there is one, is the play history.

CREDENTIALISM rewards credentials over actual capability. Society values the certificate over the skill. Polymythdnd inverts this by making the play artifact the assessment. The character sheet, the scars, the book-portal log, the homework writing — these are the credential AND the evidence of capability AND the work itself, collapsed into one artifact.

THE REPLICATION CRISIS exposes how academia rewards publishing-novel-results over generating reliable knowledge. Performance of doing-research is rewarded over actually-doing-it. Polymythdnd applies the same correction one layer down to pedagogy. Performance of learning (correct answers, sit-still-and-test) is replaced by actual-learning artifacts (the writing that resolves an in-dimension action). The teacher's narrative-judgment privilege (dm-017) probes for genuine understanding rather than testable surface compliance.

For neurodiverse students and dopamine-captured students, the framing is doubly important. Both populations are poorly served by sit-still-and-answer-the-test pedagogy. Both are well served by a play frame where engagement is the substrate of learning rather than the obstacle to it.

The between-world detail. Between books, the bookworm does the homework. The book is the reward. The reward only opens when the homework is done. The pedagogy is not adjacent to the play. It is the gate to the play.

EXTENSION:
See dm-018 teacher load-bearing, con-001 work-quality consequence. Companion concept in ml* under degorgonification section.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-023
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND five families catalog
ROLE: both

The chassis library currently identifies five families. Within a family, chassis share enough underlying math that adventures, monsters, and rulings work across members with minor adjustment. Across families, mutual exclusivity at the chassis level applies (see dm-014).

THE POPULAR FAMILY. D&D 5e, D&D 2024, Shadowdark. Mainstream lineage. Classes, levels, twenty-sided die (which polymythdnd does not use), action-and-bonus turn structure. Cousins. Adventures port between them with simple conversion. Shadowdark is the lethal-light branch.

THE OLD-SCHOOL FAMILY. BFRPG, OSE, Dolmenwood. All descend from 1980s D&D. Adventures and monsters port across with zero conversion. They differ mainly in style and setting.

THE BRUTAL-LIGHT FAMILY. Cairn, Mörk Borg. Very different aesthetics (folk-horror, doom-metal) but matching mechanical scale. One-hit kills (in single-chassis play; in polymythdnd this becomes book-death = wake in burrow per dm-015). Five-minute character creation. Adventures port with small monster adjustments.

THE TACTICAL FAMILY. Pathfinder 2 Remaster. A family of one. The three-action turn is unique to PF2R. It does not combine with any other game at the combat level — every ability is calibrated to that specific economy.

THE NARRATIVE FAMILY. Daggerheart. A family of one. The two-dice duality and narrative-tempo combat are unique. Hope and fear tokens are unique. Daggerheart is its own thing.

In polymythdnd, each family becomes a class of books. A 5e book inherits the Popular Family rails. A Cairn book inherits the Brutal-Light Family rails. The bookworm travels through the library and the AI translates the bookwormcard into each family's native idiom (see char-006).

EXTENSION:
See dm-014 chassis-of-chassis, dm-020 library-of-systems, dm-024 traveling tools, char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-024
TITLE: POLYMYTHDND ten traveling tools
ROLE: both

Ten mechanical chunks live in one chassis natively but work in any other chassis. They do not replace the underlying chassis; they sit on top of it like apps on a phone. In polymythdnd, the teacher and AI can deploy any of these in any book.

(1) THE NEGOTIATION SYSTEM. From Pathfinder 2. Replaces "roll one persuasion check" with hidden goals, weaknesses, and steady progress.

(2) THE FACTION SYSTEM. From Worlds Without Number (free). Tracks what groups in the world are doing between sessions. Their plans move forward whether the heroes intervene or not.

(3) PERSONAL VALUES PER CHARACTER. From Pathfinder 2. Each character writes down what they will always do and never do. Replaces vague alignment with concrete commitments.

(4) PERMANENT SCARS. From Cairn. When you almost die, you gain a lasting mark. Translated to polymythdnd as scars-from-books, see dm-026.

(5) THE COUNTDOWN CLOCK. From Mörk Borg. The world is ticking toward a disaster. Players do not control the tick.

(6) THE REAL-WORLD TORCH TIMER. From Shadowdark. Set a kitchen timer for one hour. When it rings, the torches go out in the dungeon.

(7) PROGRESS CLOCKS. From Blades in the Dark. Any task or threat has a clock. The clock fills with relevant actions.

(8) THE REACTION TABLE. From 1980s D&D. NPC starting attitude becomes stochastic instead of GM-decided.

(9) THE ORACLE. From Mythic Game Master Emulator. Yes/no questions answered by tables. When the GM does not want to be the one deciding, the oracle answers.

(10) THE TOKEN ECONOMY. Pick one source system's metacurrency (inspiration, hero points, hope/fear) and add it. Commit to one.

EXTENSION:
See dm-023 five families. See dm-026 scars-from-books (which formalizes scars as a polymythdnd burrow-level mechanic).

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-025
TITLE: Book portal log: traversal history record on Series II of bookwormcard
ROLE: both

Series II Page II of the bookwormcard contains the book portal log. Every book the bookworm has entered is recorded here. The log is the bookworm's traversal history.

Schema. Each row records (a) which book was entered, (b) the date entered, (c) the date emerged, (d) outcome, (e) what the trip left behind.

Outcomes enumerated. CLEARED — the bookworm completed the book's mission and left intact. GHOSTED — the bookworm's character died in the book and woke in the burrow per the Inception model (dm-015). ABANDONED — the bookworm left without completing the book. REREAD — the bookworm returned to a previously-entered book.

The active book sheet. Top of Series II Page II records the currently-loaded book. Title. Chassis. Date entered. Mission. Plus the math strip (HP, energy, tier, active modifiers) which is filled by the AI as you play and which the player and human DM do not touch.

Use in play. Teacher and AI consult the log when context matters. A bookworm who has cleared three Cairn-family books has different reflexes than one entering Cairn for the first time. The AI's contextual modifiers (dm-021) reference the log.

EXTENSION:
See dm-015 Inception death model, dm-021 AI math, char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-026
TITLE: Scars from books: Cairn scar mechanic translated to polymythdnd meta-game
ROLE: both

Cairn's scar mechanic (single-chassis: when you almost die in Cairn you gain a permanent mark) translates to polymythdnd as a meta-game mechanic. When a character nearly dies in any book and wakes in the burrow per the Inception model (dm-015), the experience leaves a mark recorded on Series II Page III of the bookwormcard.

Schema. Each scar entry records (a) which book the near-death occurred in, (b) what happened, (c) what mark it left.

Cumulative narratively. Small mechanically. Each scar individually adjusts AI math by a few percent in relevant contexts. Across many scars the cumulative effect is significant — a bookworm with twelve scars carries a noticeably different posture into the next book than a fresh bookworm.

Translation per book. The AI applies the scar contextually inside whatever book is next loaded. A scar from a Mörk Borg book where the character was nearly burned might apply as "+8% on fire-perception in any book," or as a flinch in social scenes involving open flame. The card holds the general scar; the AI translates per active book.

Why the mechanic is universal. Scars survive book transitions because they are recorded at the burrow level. The Inception model (dm-015) makes book-death recoverable but not consequence-free. Scars are the consequence-trace.

EXTENSION:
See dm-015 Inception death, dm-021 AI math, dm-024 traveling tools (item 4), char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: dm-027
TITLE: Stakes ledger: mission-failure costs at burrow level
ROLE: both

Mission failure has consequences even when character death does not (dm-015). The stakes ledger on Series II Page III of the bookwormcard records what each mission-failure cost.

Why it exists. Under the Inception model book-death is recoverable. Without stakes accumulation, mission failure would feel weightless — bookworm just dies in book, wakes in burrow, tries again. That removes meaningful stakes. The stakes ledger restores them at the burrow level.

What can be costs. Time lost in the burrow (slows access to next book). Reputation with Rainbowsol (or whoever the teacher figures as the burrow-level authority). Access to certain books (some books only open with certain reputation). Ghost-marks that linger (the bookworm is partially still in the failed book, distracted, slower to react in next books). Material loss (consumable items used in the failed attempt are gone).

Schema. Each entry records (a) what failed, (b) what it cost, (c) what now (the burrow-level state-change).

Teacher and AI roles. Teacher rules what the cost is at the moment of failure. AI records it on the ledger and applies it contextually in subsequent books.

This is where the survival-guaranteed game gets its real stakes. Character continuity is meta-stable but mission outcomes are not. Bookworms learn to care about getting it right because failure costs something they care about.

EXTENSION:
See dm-015 Inception death, dm-018 teacher load-bearing, dm-021 AI math, char-006 bookwormcard system-agnostic.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
ID: pen-013
TITLE: Name for the persistent-items class (RESOLVED, RAINBOW ITEMS)
ROLE: both

RESOLVED 2026-05-13 in the original chat then lost to PM10, re-applied 2026-05-15. The persistent-items class is named RAINBOW ITEMS. The naming follows from bw-006, the rainbow-crossing is the signature of travel back from book to burrow, so the items that survive that crossing are rainbow-items. The naming engages existing framework vocabulary rather than coining a new term. Saul-supplied source phrasing was rainbowversion which selected RAINBOW over the CONFLUENT candidate from a prior turn. The three-mode structure (dissolve, convert, remain) lives in char-005.

EXTENSION:
Status RESOLVED. Kept in PENDING section as audit-record of the ruling history.

ID: pen-014
TITLE: con-004 character-death revision to match Inception model (RESOLVED 2026-05-13)
ROLE: both

RESOLVED 2026-05-13 in the original chat then lost to PM10, re-applied 2026-05-15. con-004 was diagnosed not as a rule conflict with dm-015 but as a referent ambiguity. "Character" in con-004 referred to the polymyth-character (the smash-product on the bookwormcard, persistent across the library, e.g. capybaracowboy). dm-015 covers the book-version (the local instantiation in an active book, e.g. a regular guy in Hughes Harlem). Both rules are correct in their respective domains. Polymyth-character death stays real (burrow-level, rare). Book-version death is recoverable (the polymyth-character wakes in the burrow as a ghost in that book).

con-004 has been rewritten to surface the two-layer distinction explicitly. The two-layer ontology was already present in bw-006 (character-jewel ends at the burrow) and bw-007 (bookworm continuous, character local). pen-014 was diagnosed as a contradiction because the existing con-004 body did not name the layer it operated at.

ORIGINAL OPEN QUESTION (preserved for record). con-004 originally stated character death "stays real in bookwormburrows, not reversible through retcon or re-roll." dm-015 stated book-death is recoverable. Three options were recorded for resolution: A replace con-004 entirely, B keep con-004 and add supersede-note, C make con-004 a sub-case distinguishing single-text-dimension from multi-chassis play. Saul resolution superseded all three by diagnosing the apparent contradiction as a referent ambiguity rather than a rule conflict. The rewrite of con-004 (Option A in form but not in substance) preserves both rules at their proper layers.

EXTENSION:
Status RESOLVED. Kept in PENDING section as audit-record of the ruling history.
